--- 段落 213 (449 字元) ---
The same thing is true…  
- Marshall: The other thing I suppose is interesting about that, although I think it  sets in later in the ‘60s, when the main problem was this sense that, in the end,  the Russians were going to win.That certainly was like Henry Kissinger’s view, to  some extent.There wasn’t perhaps as much of that in the ‘50s, but if you really  took a long-term perspective, you might have even redoubled the arguments  for preemption.

[翻譯]
同一件事是真實的...
- 馬歇爾：我認為另一件有趣的事情是，儘管我認為這種想法直到60年代後期才開始盛行，當時的主要問題是，最終，俄羅斯人將贏得這場戰爭。這當然也是亨利·基辛格的觀點，某種程度上。也許在50年代時這種觀念沒有那麼普遍，但如果你真的採取了長期的視角，你可能會加倍強調先發制人的論點。

--- 段落 214 (386 字元) ---
But it was striking how poor the arguments against preemption  were.Bernard Brodie wrote a paper on the subject, and I guess one ought to go  back and reread that, but most of the argument against preemption seemed to  me very, very weak.OK.We’ve already covered some of this.Let me go back to the work with Loftus,  which really is the central matter, I think, for much of this period.

[翻譯]
但讓人驚訝的是，反對先制攻擊的論點是多麼的差勁。伯納德·布羅迪寫了一篇關於這個主題的論文，我想我應該回去重新閱讀一下，但我認為大部分反對先制攻擊的論點對我來說非常非常薄弱。好吧，我們已經討論過一些這些了。讓我回到與洛夫特斯的合作，這確實是我認為在這段時間中的很多事情的核心問題。

--- 段落 215 (385 字元) ---
I told you about  how he comes to RAND probably around ‘53, and when I had gotten back after  the six months or so teaching at Chicago.I covered the fact that we early on had come to agreement that ‘45 to ‘50 is very important for an understanding of the  Soviets.We were also convinced, as I mentioned, early on that we could do better  than the RAND people were doing on forecasting.

[翻譯]
我告訴過你，他大概在53年左右來到蘭德公司，當我在芝加哥教書六個月左右回來後。我提到我們很早就達成共識，認為了解蘇聯的‘45到‘50年是非常重要的。我們也早就相信，我們可以在預測方面做得比蘭德公司更好。

--- 段落 216 (348 字元) ---
See, one of the things that was going on at RAND at that time was that the intelligence community did not make longer-term estimates themselves.There were  a few things, but they were very limited.The RAND people who were looking at  the future, designing programs for the future, therefore were put in a position of  making up their own forecasts.

[翻譯]
看，當時蘭德公司正在進行的一件事是，情報界自己並不做出長期估計。有一些事情，但非常有限。因此，蘭德公司的人們負責展望未來、設計未來計劃，因此被迫獨自做出預測。

--- 段落 217 (464 字元) ---
Loftus and I looked at the things that they were  producing and thought that they were just awful, either because they had this  failure of this rationality model that we mentioned earlier… You had the political  scientists, who by that time were, as I said, focused on reading what the Soviets  were writing and not noticing what they were doing, and they were not a basis  for anything.But then you had people probably over-inventive on the side of the  Soviets.

[翻譯]
羅夫特斯和我看著他們正在生產的東西，覺得它們簡直糟糕透了，要不然就是因為他們早前提到的邏輯模型出現了失敗……當時的政治學家們，如我所說的，專注於閱讀蘇聯人寫的東西，卻沒有注意到他們正在做什麼，這對任何事情都沒有基礎。但與此同時，蘇聯人可能在發明方面過於過分。

--- 段落 218 (372 字元) ---
An example of which was—I think one of the things that, at least at RAND,  very much set back analyses in the air defense area—And something you have  to remember is that in the ‘50s, the U.S.had a very vigorous program to build up  its air defenses.In fact, I think that by the end of the ‘50s, we were spending more  on air defenses than we were on the strategic forces.

[翻譯]
舉一個例子來說，我認為至少在蘭德公司，極大地影響了空防領域分析的一件事是，您必須記住的是，在50年代，美國有一個非常積極的計劃來建立其空防。事實上，我認為到50年代末，我們在空防方面的支出比戰略力量還要多。

--- 段落 219 (462 字元) ---
66 But as the RAND people  got into this in the middle ‘50s or so… And by the way, they did for a while have  a very interesting behavioral scientist, a psychologist named John Kennedy, who  developed some very good simulation stuff, which then spun off into that…  
- Q2: SDC?- Marshall: …SDC [System Development Corporation], which did some very interesting things.67  But the people, in doing their analyses, were super-inventive on the part of the  Russians.

[翻譯]
但是當蘭德研究院在50年代中期左右開始參與這個領域時… 順便說一下，他們一度有一位非常有趣的行為科學家，一位名叫約翰·肯尼迪的心理學家，他開發了一些非常好的模擬工具，後來衍生出…  
- 問題2：SDC? - 馬歇爾：…SDC（系統開發公司），做了一些非常有趣的事情。但是在做他們的分析時，對俄羅斯人表現出超級創造力。

--- 段落 220 (484 字元) ---
I mean, at the radar perimeter, they had the Russians’ bombers coming  in with thousands of decoys and cruise missiles.In fact, cruise missiles initially  were largely invented as bomber decoys.That’s the way our thinking was.It was  only in probably the early ‘60s that people like Al Latter and company said, “Why  don’t we put bombs on these things?” which was a heresy in the eyes of the Air  Force.Anyway, they made the problem so hard that you just couldn’t defend  the country.

[翻譯]
我的意思是，在雷達周邊，他們發現俄羅斯的轟炸機帶著成千上萬的假裝目標和巡航導彈。事實上，巡航導彈最初主要是作為轟炸機的假裝目標而發明的。這就是我們當時的想法。直到大約60年代初，像阿爾·拉特爾等人才說：“我們為什麼不把炸彈放在這些東西上？”這在空軍眼中是異端邪說。無論如何，他們使問題變得如此困難，以至於你無法保衛這個國家。

--- 段落 221 (478 字元) ---
You always kept getting the answer that it was nearly impossible.It  wasn’t clear that that was really ever true.68  Anyway, Loftus and I didn’t think much of what they were doing, so we undertook  our own project, probably after another thing I worked on a lot, but which was  not that intellectually important—work on strategic warning.69 We started this  project called “Sovoy,” in which we offered to start making projections for the rest  of RAND.70  
- Q4: Of the Soviets?

[翻譯]
你總是得到的答案是幾乎不可能。但很不清楚那是真的。 68 無論如何，羅夫特斯和我對他們所做的事情不以為然，所以我們開始了我們自己的項目，可能是在我致力於另一項重要但不那麼有智力價值的工作之後，即戰略預警。 我們開始了這個名為“Sovoy”的項目，我們提議為其他蘭德機構開始做預測。- 蘇聯的預測？

--- 段落 222 (485 字元) ---
- Marshall: On the Soviets.- Q2: Using classified information?- Marshall: Yeah.- Q2: I mean using everything you had.- Marshall: Yes, right.In fact, we had created a special arrangement with the intelligence people at the analytic level to give us much more material than they  otherwise would, because of our own connections with these guys, especially  Loftus’s.Then we got to this problem of, “How are we going to do this?” Then you  get to the things that I was mentioning earlier.

[翻譯]
- 馬歇爾：談到蘇聯。- Q2：使用機密信息嗎？- 馬歇爾：是的。- Q2：我的意思是利用你所擁有的一切。- 馬歇爾：對的。事實上，我們已經與情報人員在分析層面建立了特殊安排，讓他們給我們比平常更多的資料，這是因為我們與這些人的聯繫，特別是羅夫特斯的。然後我們遇到了這個問題，“我們該怎麼辦？”然後你會討論到我之前提到的事情。

--- 段落 223 (420 字元) ---
Loftus and I already believed that  you need to know all about the history of these organizations and where they  come from.It’s an important fact, for example, that the Soviet missile people [the  Strategic Rocket Forces], when they were formed, took over one of the existing  academies—What do you think it was?It was the artillery academy.So you’ve got  to know about these guys, where they’re corning from and so on.

[翻譯]
Loftus和我已經相信，你需要知道這些組織的歷史以及它們的來歷。例如，蘇聯的導彈人員（戰略火箭軍）成立時，接管了一所現有的學院-你認為是什麼學院？那是砲兵學院。所以你必須了解這些人的背景，他們來自哪裡等等。

--- 段落 224 (395 字元) ---
And then I have  this, as I said, blindingly obvious insight of, “They’re organizations.That’s what  we’re trying to predict the behavior of.” Then you get into, “What the hell do we  know about organizations?”  So I start to read—this all starts about the spring of ‘57, probably, or ‘56 sometime—Chester Barnard, Herbert Simon [Administrative Behavior], Simon and  James March [Organizations].

[翻譯]
然後，正如我所說的那樣，我突然非常明顯地意識到，“它們是組織。這就是我們試圖預測行為的對象。”然後你開始思考，“我們對組織了解得有多少呢？”所以我開始閱讀——這大概是在1957年春季左右開始的，或者可能是1956年——查斯特·巴納德、赫伯特·西蒙《行政行為》，西蒙和詹姆斯·馬奇《組織》。

--- 段落 225 (399 字元) ---
Later, when it comes out, Richard Cyert and March  [Behavioral Theory of the Firm], which was probably the most influential book for  me.And then later, when Crozier comes out in ‘63 with his book, I read that.71  
- Q3: The Bureaucratic Phenomenon.- Marshall: Yeah, right.And this really was the central part of the stuff I worked on, except for when I went away to the Gaither Committee and so on.

[翻譯]
後來，《行為理論公司》一書出版時，這可能對我影響最大。後來，當克羅吉爾在63年出版他的書時，我也讀了那本書。這確實是我研究的重要部分，除了當我去參加蓋瑟委員會等活動時。

--- 段落 226 (408 字元) ---
But until I left for  Paris, my work was on how do we do a better job of understanding the Soviets,  predicting them, thinking about them [indistinct], with this matter of, “We’ve got  to understand the allocation of resources, what their constraints are, what the  long-term costs are of the level of effort they put into the military,” and so on.That reminds me of another thing I did around the late ‘50s.

[翻譯]
但直到我去巴黎之前，我的工作一直在探討如何更好地了解蘇聯、預測他們、思考他們，這涉及「我們必須了解資源的分配情況，他們的限制是什麼，他們投入軍事的努力所帶來的長期成本是多少」等問題。這讓我想起了我在50年代後期所做的另一件事。

--- 段落 227 (399 字元) ---
I did a lot of work on  the accuracy of our cost estimates of our own programs at various stages.You find  out the early estimates were pretty lousy.72  One other thing is this collaboration with Herb about deterrence and war-fighting,  which looked at the contrasting utility functions of ourselves and the Russians at  various stages of the exchanges that may go on.73  So then I go away to Paris.

[翻譯]
我在不同階段對我們自己項目的成本估算準確性進行了大量工作。你會發現初步估算相當糟糕。另一件事是我與Herb合作討論威懾和交戰，探討我們和俄羅斯在可能進行的交流過程中的對比效用。然後我前往巴黎。

--- 段落 228 (385 字元) ---
Pleasant living, no intellectual content, and learn more  about how abysmal organizations can be, how whole organizations can exist and  do practically nothing with lots of people paid a lot of money.- Q3: Were you sent there or…?- Marshall: Yes.What happened was Secretary of Defense Robert McNamara came  to an agreement with Dirk Stikker, who was then the Secretary General of NATO.

[翻譯]
宜居舒適，缺乏智力內容，更了解組織有多糟糕，整個組織如何存在並幾乎不做任何事情，卻有許多人得到高薪。問題三：你是被派到那裡去的還是…？馬歇爾：是的。發生的事情是國防部長羅伯特·麥克納馬拉與當時北約秘書長德克·斯蒂克達達成了一項協議。

--- 段落 229 (438 字元) ---
It was in ‘65 that there was going to be a five-year review process of the programs  within NATO, or there was then.McNamara persuaded Stikker that, “Look, this  thing is corning up in ‘65.What we should do is have some studies done so that  when we come to this review, we have some basis for deciding what’s good,  what’s bad.”  
- Q4: Revolutionary concept.- Marshall: So he approached RAND to put together a team of people to go over.

[翻譯]
在1965年時，北約計劃進行為期五年的審查程序，或當時正進行。麥克納馬拉說服史迪克認為，“看，這件事在1965年要發生。我們應該讓一些研究進行，這樣到時候進行審查時，我們就有一些基礎來決定什麼是好的，什麼是壞的。”馬歇爾：這是一個革命性的概念。於是他找來蘭德研究所組織一個團隊進行審查。

--- 段落 230 (405 字元) ---
It was headed by a guy from RAND who was then the head of the Economics  Department, Burt Klein, and included me, Fred Hoffman, and Oleg Hoeffding, and  Peter Szanton, who was in the government at the time, came and that was it.We  were to do these collaborative studies with the other countries.74 I worked with  a succession of French colonels who, for a variety of reasons, were the head of  the thing.

[翻譯]
這個小組由當時是經濟學系主任的RAND機構的一位負責人柏特·克萊恩領導，還有我、弗雷德·霍夫曼、奧列格·赫夫丁和當時在政府工作的皮特·薩松。我們被要求和其他國家進行這些合作研究。我曾和一系列法國上校合作，這些人因各種原因成為該小組的負責人。

--- 段落 231 (439 字元) ---
The study that I did looked at the actual stockpiles of ammunition and  other things, like tanks, that were held as replacements for attrition or for expenditure in war.There was a set of standards that people were supposed to have, so  many days of supply and so on and so forth.This was an across-theboard study of,  “What did people actually have?” Right.- Q3: I was just wondering if you volunteered for this or were…  
- Marshall: No.

[翻譯]
我所進行的研究觀察了實際的彈藥庫存量，以及其他替代品，如坦克，這些替代品用於戰爭中的消耗。人們應該擁有一套標準，例如供應的天數等等。這是一項全面性的研究，“人們實際擁有什麼？”對了。- Q3：我只是想知道你是自願參加的還是... 
- 馬歇爾：不是。

--- 段落 232 (455 字元) ---
I was asked because by that time I had done some studies on NATO  problems.When I returned in the spring of ‘65, the thing I then proposed was that I organize  a program of study at RAND on organizational behavior and how our knowledge  of that could be used in a wide variety of things, including this business of understanding the Russians.75 I was allowed to do that, to use not only my own time,  but to get three or four other people to work with me.

[翻譯]
在那個時候我被要求是因為我已經做了一些有關北約問題的研究。當我在1965年春季回來時，我當時提出的建議是在蘭德公司組織一個研究計劃，研究組織行為以及我們如何利用這方面的知識來應用在各種事物上，包括理解俄羅斯人。我被允許這樣做，不僅可以利用自己的時間，還可以讓另外三四個人和我一起工作。

--- 段落 233 (300 字元) ---
Because of that, I first met  Jim March of Carnegie-Mellon University, and from him got leads to some students who might be recruited.Pat Crecine came for a year because of that.I went  to Harvard and talked with Dick Neustadt.I was told I ought to do that because  of some of the stuff he was doing.

[翻譯]
因此，我第一次遇到了卡內基美隆大學的吉姆·馬奇，從他那裡得到了一些可能被招募的學生的線索。帕特·克里辛因此來了一年。我去了哈佛大學，與狄克·諾伊斯達特交談。有人告诉我应该这样做，因为他正在做的一些事情。

--- 段落 234 (468 字元) ---
Out of that came the creation of the so-called  “May Group” chaired by Professor Ernest May, which began to meet probably  in the fall of ‘65, to talk not only about organizational behavior, but this whole  business of how do you understand the behavior of governments, governmental  organizations.Graham Allison was his research assistant, or some associate of  his, and was the rapporteur of the group.And out of that in some ways came the  book Essence of Decision.

[翻譯]
隨之而來的是由歐內斯特·梅教授主持的所謂“五月集團”的創立，該組織很可能在1965年秋季開始舉行會議，討論的不僅僅是組織行為，還包括如何理解政府及政府組織的行為。格雷厄姆·艾利森是他的研究助理，或是他的一位助手，也是該組織的記錄者。在某種程度上，這促成了《決策的要義》這本書的出版。

--- 段落 235 (490 字元) ---
76 When I started to look at this business about organizational behavior, I looked around and located this cluster of people at Carnegie  that was intellectually attracted to it.Then I went and talked to the people at the  Harvard Business School to see what they were doing about trying to understand  organizational behavior.It was there that I came upon these notions of strategy  that they were developing.And both of those things had, I think, a really big  impact on what I did later.

[翻譯]
當我開始研究組織行為的業務時，我四處打聽，發現在卡內基有一群對此感興趣的人。然後我去和哈佛商學院的人談話，看看他們對於理解組織行為做了什麼。在那裡，我接觸到了他們正在發展的戰略概念。這兩件事對我之後的工作影響很大，我認為。

--- 段落 236 (489 字元) ---
The other thing that happened about that time—some of it predates my going off  to Paris—was that James Schlesinger had come to RAND to spend a summer in ‘62,  I believe, and we became acquainted and friends.Then he came back as a fulltime person just about the time I was leaving for Paris [summer 1963].But after I returned, I spent a lot of time talking with him.One of the things that the two of us  read, about somewhere in that period, was Robert Ardrey’s The Territorial Imperative.

[翻譯]
大約在那個時候發生的另一件事情——有些事情發生在我去巴黎之前——是詹姆斯·施萊辛格在1962年夏天來RAND度假，我認為是那一年，我們成為了熟識的朋友。後來他回來成為一名全職人員，差不多就在我離開去巴黎的時候[1963年夏天]。但是我回來後，花了很多時間與他交談。在那段時期，我們兩個人讀的其中一本書是羅伯特·阿德里的《領土本能》。

--- 段落 237 (431 字元) ---
77  And I got very interested in, “Here’s another way of thinking about human beings  and how they behave.” Still later, and not so much based on Ardrey’s stuff, but on  the work of other people, I became further interested in these nonrational aspects  of behavior.And I arrived at this notion that maybe RAND is not a rational animal.- Q4: That’s it right there.- Marshall: And there are interesting things to be said about that.

[翻譯]
77我對「這是另一種思考人類和他們行為方式的方式」非常感興趣。稍後，不太基於阿德利的東西，而是基於其他人的工作，我對行為的非理性方面更感興趣。我得出這樣的觀念，或許人類不是理性動物。- 問題4：就在這裡。- 馬歇爾：關於這一點有許多有趣的事情可以談論。

--- 段落 238 (242 字元) ---
Also, Schlesinger  and I began to talk, probably in the ‘68–‘69 period, about the implications of all of  that stuff that Ardrey and others were doing by that time.I’m thinking about the  psychological and political impact of military forces.

[翻譯]
此外，施萊辛格和我在大約1968年至1969年期間開始討論阿德瑞和其他人當時所進行的所有研究的影響。我在思考軍事力量的心理和政治影響。

--- 段落 239 (430 字元) ---
So it seems to me, intellectually, the organizational, behavioral stuff, plus Crozier’s  connection of the organizational stuff to culture, and this ethology, led me to this  low opinion or critique of the standard deterrence theories, the whole rational actor  view.And, of course, I obviously, from the ‘50s, was already a little skeptical about  rationality as a way of thinking about what people do or predicting what they do.

[翻譯]
所以在我的理智看來，組織和行為的事情，再加上克羅齊爾將組織事務與文化聯繫起來的這個觀點，以及這種行為學，讓我對標準威懾理論，整個理性行為者觀點持有低評價或批評。當然，我從50年代开始就對理性作為思考人們行為或預測人們行為的方式持有一些質疑。

--- 段落 240 (336 字元) ---
Then, I don’t understand exactly now why I wrote that ‘66 paper on assessing military power [Problems of Estimating Military Power].78 I was encouraged to do it by  Bill Kaufmann for some political science association meeting here in Washington  [the paper says, “American Political Science Meetings in New York, September 6–9,  1966”].

[翻譯]
然後，我現在不確切明白為什麼我寫了那篇關於評估軍事力量的論文[評估軍事力量的問題]。我是在華盛頓某次政治科學協會會議中受到Bill Kaufmann的鼓勵寫這篇論文的。該論文上寫著“1966年9月6日至9日在紐約舉行的美國政治科學會議”。

--- 段落 241 (441 字元) ---
1966 seems early to me, at least in terms of my memory, because—maybe  it happened earlier than I thought—Fred Wikner, who I don’t know if some of  you know, visited RAND to obtain analytic support for his work.There had been  created here in the Defense Department a Net Technical Assessment function.He came to RAND, but my memory of it is that this was probably ‘67, ‘68 [not ‘66,  when Problems of Estimating Military Power was written].

[翻譯]
對我來說，1966年似乎很早，至少在我記憶中是這樣，因為也許這比我想像中的要早一些，弗雷德·維克納（Fred Wikner）來到藍德公司尋求分析支持他的工作。國防部已經成立了一個網絡技術評估功能。他來到了藍德公司，但我記得這可能是在1967年或1968年，而不是1966年（《估計軍事實力問題》編寫時）。

--- 段落 242 (462 字元) ---
And I started to do a little  work for him on a contract about, “How do you do net technical assessments?How would you really think about that?”79 Anyway, the chronology here may be  wrong, and something that one needs to check.- Q2: He came out to RAND in ‘67, ‘68 and asked you to start working on this?- Marshall: Yeah.- Q2: So it was created in ‘64, ‘65?- Marshall: I don’t know.That’s something that needs to be checked.I don’t know  what the chronology is.

[翻譯]
我開始為他做一點點關於簽約的工作，“如何進行網路技術評估？你真的如何思考這個問題？”不論如何，在這裡的年代順序可能是錯誤的，這是需要檢查的事情。- Q2: 他在‘67年，‘68年來到蘭德公司，並要求你開始這項工作？- 馬歇爾： 是的。- Q2: 那麼這是在‘64年，‘65年創建的嗎？- 馬歇爾： 我不知道。這是需要檢查的事情。我不知道時間順序是什麼。

--- 段落 243 (456 字元) ---
My guess is the earliest it probably was created was ‘66.80  But I don’t know whether one of the reasons for writing that…paper on assessing  the military balance [Problems of Estimating Military Power] was to support Wikner.I just can’t remember why I did that.I guess something I need to do is to go back  and look at the papers I wrote for Wikner.Also something that happened about this time is Harry Rowen became the president of RAND, sometime in ‘67.

[翻譯]
我猜測最早創建的可能是'66.80。但我不知道寫那篇關於評估軍事平衡的論文[《估算軍事力量的問題》]是否其中一個原因是為了支持Wikner。我只是不記得我當時為什麼這麼做。我想我需要做的一件事是回去看我為Wikner寫的那些論文。同時，大約在'67年，哈利·羅文成為了蘭德公司的總裁。

--- 段落 244 (406 字元) ---
Jim Schlesinger and I used to spend a lot of time  with him because both of us thought there were a lot of problems at RAND and  that maybe he was going to fix them.81 It didn’t happen that way, but… One of  the things that did was lead to this creation of a new post of Director of Strategic  Studies—that is, dealing with strategic forces—that Schlesinger took over in  probably the spring of ‘68 [1967].

[翻譯]
Jim Schlesinger和我過去常花很多時間與他在一起，因為我們都認為蘭德研究所存在許多問題，也許他能解決這些問題。然而事情並沒有這樣發展，但有一件事是導致了一個新的戰略研究主任職位的產生 - 即處理戰略力量的職位 - 而舽辛格可能在1968年春季接任這個職位。

--- 段落 245 (491 字元) ---
82  Then Schlesinger left RAND in very late ‘68 to rejoin some of the transition teams  in the turnover that was taking place to the Nixon Administration, and then left  permanently in January of ‘69.Rowen asked me to take over the position of Director of Strategic Studies, which led to my doing a lot of thinking about the strategic program.Out of that came this thing that I wrote on the long-term competition  [Long-Term Competition with the Soviets: A Framework for Strategic Analysis].

[翻譯]
在1968年末，舒萊辛格離開了蘭德公司，重新加入了一些轉型團隊，參與尼克松政府的交接，然後在1969年1月永久離開。羅溫要求我接任戰略研究主任一職，這促使我對戰略計劃進行了很多思考。在這個過程中，我寫了一篇長期競爭與蘇聯的論述，這篇文章最終成形為《與蘇聯的長期競爭：戰略分析框架》。

--- 段落 246 (421 字元) ---
83  I guess I was moved to do that because when I looked at what people were working on at RAND with respect to strategic forces, it just seemed kind of a mishmash  of all kinds of things.So I tried to address the question, “What if you really had  some sort of program that had some intellectual strategy to it?What should it  look like?” And so I addressed the question of, “How should you think about strategic forces?

[翻譯]
我想我之所以會被感動做這件事，是因為當我看到蘭德研究所的人們在戰略力量方面的工作時，這似乎就像是各種事物的混合。因此，我嘗試回答這個問題：“如果你真的有某種具有思想策略的計畫，它應該是什麼樣子？”所以我討論了這個問題：“你應該如何思考戰略力量？”

--- 段落 247 (487 字元) ---
” Then the things that came back to me were, first, these ideas from  the early ‘50s of, you’re in an extended competition with the other side.Then,  from the Harvard Business School stuff that I had been spending a lot of time  on since the middle ‘60s, comes this notion, you should have a strategy for this  competition.And one of the things you want to focus on are your strengths and  weaknesses, his strengths and weaknesses.One of your objectives is to drive him  out of business.

[翻譯]
接著讓我回想起的事情是，首先是來自50年代初的這些想法，你正在和對手進行一場延續性的競爭。然後，自從60年代中期開始我一直花了很多時間研究哈佛商學院的一些東西，這個概念就是，你應該為這場競爭制定一個策略。而其中一個你要專注的事情是你的優勢和劣勢，他的優勢和劣勢。你的一個目標是要將他逼出市場。

--- 段落 248 (456 字元) ---
There may be some risks in doing some things too hastily, and  you want to look at that.And then, what you’re talking about are organizations,  and they have all kinds of built-in vulnerabilities, problems that they can’t correct  very easily, and so there may be things you can exploit.I just had this sense that this is a terrific new way of looking at these things.At  one level, it all seems to me very obvious—yes, you should look at things like that.

[翻譯]
在做一些事情時太草率可能存在一些風險，你要考慮這一點。然後，你所談論的是組織，它們有各種內在脆弱性和難以輕易解決的問題，因此可能有一些你可以利用的事情。我只是覺得這是一種看待這些事情的絕佳新方式。在某種程度上，對我來說這一切都顯得非常明顯 - 是的，你應該像這樣看待事情。

--- 段落 249 (450 字元) ---
And it’s odd, as I say, that some of the people at RAND in the early years had some  of these views although they weren’t integrating them with these ideas on the  behavior of organizations and so on.It’s just odd to me, as I think about it, that  this kind of perspective just disappeared from the middle ‘50s until the late ‘60s.And so that’s what I have to say on that, I think.We can take it up later.But let me  just run over a couple of things.

[翻譯]
在我看來，蘭德研究所的一些人在早期年份中有一些這些觀點，儘管他們並沒有將這些觀點與組織行為等方面的想法整合在一起。我認為這是有些奇怪的，當我想想時，這種觀點在50年代中期消失，直到60年代末才重新出現。這就是我對此的看法，我想我們可以稍後再討論。但讓我簡單講述一下幾點。

--- 段落 250 (432 字元) ---
What about the contrast with the mainline thinking at RAND?One contrast is,  and we’ve talked about it already: I believed counterforce was possible.During  much of the time, people at RAND didn’t.84 Even the shooting down of the U-2  didn’t really make people feel that it was entirely possible, although it shifted the  balance of argument.- Q3: Could you expand on that a little bit, the shooting down of the U-2 and its  effect?

[翻譯]
在蘭德公司的主要思維與這種對比如何?其中一種對比是，而且我們已經討論過:我相信反制打擊是可能的。在很長一段時間裡，蘭德公司的人們並不這麼認為。即使U-2被擊落也並沒有讓人們完全感到可能性，盡管它轉變了論點的平衡。- Q3:你能稍微擴展一下，U-2被擊落的事件及其影響?

--- 段落 251 (398 字元) ---
- Marshall: It made public the fact that you had this reconnaissance thing.And, in  fact, I remember Alain Enthoven stopping me in the parking lot and saying something like, “Now I understand why you’ve been…”85  Most of the rest of my outline we’ve already talked about.Let me just end with  some comments about the national level or the more general things.It’s something I’ve talked a lot about.

[翻譯]
馬歇爾：這個公開了你進行偵察活動的事實。實際上，我記得艾林·恩索温在停車場拦住我，說了一句類似“現在我明白你為什麼一直……”的話。我們已經談過我的大部分大綱了，讓我就以一些有關國家層面或更一般的事情的評論作結。這是我談過很多次的事情。

--- 段落 252 (474 字元) ---
I think World War II and the kind of generation of  people who came out of it, who played an important role, already had some  important level of participation in it, are very important.It had a big impact, I  think, on the character of the thinking of the people at RAND.It had an impact on  those who had come from that the World War II experience, somebody like Hitch,  for example, or people in the Eisenhower Administration—I think there were a lot  of the same people.

[翻譯]
我認為第二次世界大戰以及其中涌現的那一代人，他們在其中扮演重要角色，已經參與了一些很重要的活動，這是非常重要的。我認為這對蘭德研究所的人的思維特徵有很大影響。對於那些經歷過第二次世界大戰的人，像是希奇（Hitch）這樣的人，或是艾森豪威爾政府中的人，我認為有很多相同的人。

--- 段落 253 (299 字元) ---
I think it needs to be articulated and understood, but I just have the feeling that people who went through that in some responsible position  just came away with a sense of, life is serious, you make decisions, if you have a  problem you think about it, and then you decide what you’re going to do.

[翻譯]
我認為這需要被表達和理解，但我只是有種感覺，那些在某個負責的職位上經歷過這些事情的人，只是帶著一種生活很認真的感覺，你必須做決定，如果你遇到問題，你要好好思考，然後再決定你要怎麼做。

--- 段落 254 (496 字元) ---
The reason I raise that is I think that in the Eisenhower period, when you had this big  shift taking place that we talked about earlier, because of the growth of the nuclear  stockpiles on both sides, there was a whole succession of special study groups and  so on.It seems to me symptomatic that soon after a problem was surfaced, a serious group of people was put together to look at it and they came up with suggestions.The suggestions were not always followed, but the issues were addressed.

[翻譯]
我提出這個問題的原因是我認為在艾森豪威爾時代，正如我們之前討論的那樣，由於雙方核庫存的增長，發生了一個重大轉變。這時出現了一系列特別的研究小組等等。在問題浮現不久之後，一群嚴肅的人被組織在一起來研究這個問題，他們提出了建議。這些建議並不總是被采納，但問題得到了解決。

--- 段落 255 (419 字元) ---
There was also in the Eisenhower period this whole notion of an extended  competition.For example, the question of, “Should we overspend?” There was a  longer-term perspective, particularly in the early years.I think, given the performance of the U.S.government from the early ‘60s on, the work in the ‘50s is  impressive to me.Maybe if you look back in detail it wouldn’t come out that way,  but that’s the way I feel.

[翻譯]
在艾森豪時期，還有這個整體概念，即延續比賽的想法。例如，“我們應該超支嗎？”特別是在早期，有一個長期的視角。我認為，從60年代初開始，美國政府的表現給我留下了深刻的印象。也許如果你仔細回顧，就不會這樣，但這就是我的感覺。

--- 段落 256 (476 字元) ---
It’s certainly different in my view, than in the late ‘60s, early ‘70s, when you have  this final kind of coming to terms, in a certain sense, with strategic parity.Here we  were, we had an overall strategy relative to the Russians, particularly in our alliance arrangements and so on, that in some ways depended on an advantage in  strategic weaponry.Parity happens, and there is no reconsideration of, “Now we  have a different situation, should we do something differently?

[翻譯]
依我看，現在與60年代末、70年代初有很大不同，那時我們正面對戰略平衡的情況。我們當時與俄羅斯人有一個整體上的戰略，特別是我們的聯盟安排等，在某種程度上依賴於戰略武器上的優勢。當平衡出現時，並沒有重新考慮，"現在我們處於不同的情況，應該做些不同的事情嗎？"

--- 段落 257 (329 字元) ---
Do we now have  to have a different balance in conventional forces?” Never even addressed.And  when the people were writing Henry Kissinger’s memoirs on this period, I asked  them, Peter Rodman and Bill Hyland—and I was there part of that time—“Was  this issue ever raised?” Their answer was, basically, they saw no record of it.

[翻譯]
我們現在是否需要在常規武力方面取得不同的平衡？這個問題甚至沒有被提及。當人們在寫亨利·基辛格在這個時期的回憶錄時，我詢問他們，彼得·羅德曼和比爾·海蘭德，我當時也在場，“這個問題是否被提出過？” 他們的答案基本上是他們沒有看到任何記錄。

--- 段落 258 (463 字元) ---
86  Now it seems to me, in addition, of course, that another period that deserves a lot  of study is the period around ‘63, ‘64, where in the aftermath of the Cuban missile  crisis I think there was just a big shift.I don’t know whether it was that people  found that experience on reflection or even at the time so terrifying that they  never wanted to be anywhere as near as close that they thought they might be  to real war, but I think there was a big shift.

[翻譯]
現在，在我看來，另一個值得深入研究的時期是在‘63年、‘64年左右，在古巴危機後，我認為這是一個重大的轉變。我不知道是不是人們在回顧那段經歷或甚至在當時覺得那麼可怕，以至於他們從未想過會接近真正的戰爭，但我認為當時發生了重大轉變。

--- 段落 259 (457 字元) ---
Kennedy came in on the argument  that Eisenhower wasn’t doing enough, that we’ve got to up the budget, we’ve  got to compete more effectively, and so on, and all of a sudden there’s this switch  and we’re into arms control, settling for parity and even, to some extent in the  administration, but certainly later in the Congress, there were these regulations,  stipulations, limits on the accuracy of our weapons so that we don’t threaten the  Soviet silos.

[翻譯]
肯尼迪加入了爭論，認為艾森豪威爾並未做足夠的努力，我們必須增加預算，我們必須更有效地競爭，突然之間，我們轉而討論軍備控制，追求平衡，甚至在政府內部某種程度上，但肯定是稍後在國會中，對我們武器的準確性設定了這些規定、規定和限制，以便我們不會威脅蘇聯的地下發射井。

--- 段落 260 (107 字元) ---
87 There was a whole set of decisions which are, in my view, anti-strategic or represented a loss of nerve.

[翻譯]
在我看來，有一整套決策是反戰略的，或者表示了一種失去勇氣的損失。

--- 段落 261 (426 字元) ---
And so there was a period in there when we  were, in some sense, allowing the Soviets to impose costs on us by the increases  they were making in the accuracy of their weapons and retrofit programs and  so on, increases in hardness and some other things, efforts to begin looking at  global missiles and so on, while we were abstaining from imposing similar costs  on them as “unfair,” “destabilizing,” and all that horseshit.

[翻譯]
因此，在某種意義上，有一段時間我們允許蘇聯通過提高其武器精確度、改裝計劃等方面的增加成本來對我們造成影響，同時我們卻避免對他們施加類似的成本，認為這是“不公平”的、“破壞穩定”的等等胡扯。

--- 段落 262 (437 字元) ---
So I think—I’m never going to do that—but I keep proposing to people that they  really look at that, these special aspects of the people, the generation from World War II, this kind of critical period in the early ‘60s, when I think there was a kind of  flip-flop, switch…loss of nerve, really.Then there was also, when you get to Kissinger—it isn’t that he’s to be picked  on—this wide class of people with this pessimism about the U.S.

[翻譯]
所以我認為 - 我永遠不會這樣做 - 但我不斷建議人們真正看待這一點，這些特殊方面的人，第二次世界大戰的一代人，這種在六十年代初的關鍵時期，當時我認為真的是一種轉變、猶豫、真的是失去勇氣。然後也有，當你談到基辛格時 - 並不是他是要受到攻擊的 - 這一大群對美國感到悲觀的人。

--- 段落 263 (440 字元) ---
competing with  the Russians over the long term, which is one of the fruits of this absolutely awful  effort by not just the CIA, but almost the whole of academia, on the Russian economy—its problems, the size of the military burden, and all of those things.I think  it’s really true that Henry saw himself, with what he thought of as kind of an idiotic  populace, making the best deal with this power that was going to dominate inevitably.

[翻譯]
與俄羅斯長期競爭，這是不僅是美國中央情報局，幾乎整個學術界對俄羅斯經濟、問題、軍事負擔規模等進行了絕對可怕努力的成果之一。我認為，亨利認為自己在與這個必然主宰的力量達成最好交易，看到自己身處的某種白癡大眾。

--- 段落 264 (476 字元) ---
The thing that differentiated Schlesinger from him was…  In fact, I remember in a Time article [11 Feb ‘74] there was a little box in the middle  of the article which had one of the most significant statements by Schlesinger—  but most people don’t pay any attention to it—that he saw himself as a “revivalist,”  getting people’s spirits up.88 Why the hell should we lose?He certainly didn’t think  that we were going to necessarily lose.But there certainly was a lot of that.

[翻譯]
將Schlesinger與他區分開來的是... 實際上，我記得在一篇《時代》文章（1974年2月11日）中，文章中間有一個小框框，其中有Schlesinger做出的最重要的一句話 - 但大多數人沒有注意到 - 他看到自己是一個"復興者"，可以振奮人們的精神。為什麼我們應該輸？他肯定沒有認為我們必然會輸。但確實有很多這種想法。

--- 段落 265 (428 字元) ---
And I think you can’t understand why these analyses of the Soviet economy and  other things were so lousy unless you go back to the ‘30s and the ‘40s and the  generation of people who came along and dominated much of the economics  profession and certainly did not believe in free markets.- Q2: How would you weigh that in relation to this sense that there was a sort of lost  faith in America and American ideals after Vietnam?

Therefore the Russians, because they have a planned system will work better than… Is that kind of…  
- Marshall: Yeah, that’s right.See, it’s a goddam scandal, I think, the way that G.Warren  Nutter was treated.When you read his book now—it’s true he spoke more vigorously—but the book itself is the mildest statement of … poses the question, What  reason is there to believe that in the longer term the centrally managed economy  will grow faster than the free economy?

--- 段落 270 (435 字元) ---
90 He put a lot of information on the table  that suggested there wasn’t any reason.But he was seen as an absolute ideologue  and really excluded from first-rate universities.He just wouldn’t be considered for  Yale or places like that.And for that reason, this guy ended up at the University of  Virginia.It’s these other guys who are the ideologues, the whole bunch of them,  largely, and even at RAND, somebody as sensible as Hitch.

[翻譯]
他將許多顯示沒有任何理由的資訊放在桌上。但他被視為絕對的意識形態學者，真的被一流大學排除在外。他根本不會被考慮進入耶魯大學或類似的地方。因此，這個人最終進入了維吉尼亞大學。這些其他人才是意識形態學者，他們大部分人，在蘭德公司，甚至像希奇這樣明智的人。

--- 段落 271 (450 字元) ---
I think it was Allen  Wallis who was telling me about how the criticism that was made of the RAND  economics effort on the Soviet Union…which was a whole bunch of people, Abe  Bergson-trained people, violently…treated any criticism as being ideological,  when the fact was here were these guys with all their few suppositions….One of the things I guess I forgot to comment on: Here Loftus and I were trying to  get this work done, do this projection.

[翻譯]
我想是艾倫·沃利斯告訴我蘭德經濟學研究對蘇聯的批評是如何被一眾亞伯·伯格森的人激烈地視為意識形態問題，當時這些人們有他們的一些假設...我猜我忘了評論的一件事：Loftus和我試圖完成這項工作，做這個預測。

--- 段落 272 (497 字元) ---
We would come to RAND economists analyzing the Soviet economy and ask them questions.In the first place, they had no  answers, or didn’t even want to work on any serious problems.And they claimed,  “Oh, we can’t make answers to questions like that.” I guess that led me, along with  other times, to have this view that poor answers to good questions are a lot more  valuable than good answers to poor questions.These, we thought, were the good  questions that people really ought to be working on.

[翻譯]
我們會找來蘭德經濟學家來分析蘇聯經濟，並向他們提問。起初，他們沒有答案，甚至不願意處理任何嚴肅的問題。他們聲稱：“哦，我們無法對這樣的問題做出答案。”我想這讓我們，和其他時候一樣，對於好問題的差答案比對於爛問題的好答案更有價值這個觀點。這些，我們認為，是人們真正應該努力解決的好問題。

--- 段落 273 (355 字元) ---
But you couldn’t get any of  those guys to even address them.They had their things.These people were not  only worthless on the few questions, but had over time, I think, perpetrated this  view of the Soviets as constantly growing, a very inflated view of their GNP, while  simultaneously underestimating the size of the resources going into the military.

[翻譯]
但你無法讓這些人提及這些問題。他們有自己的理念。這些人不僅在少數問題上毫無價值，而且隨著時間的推移，我認為，對蘇聯的看法是不斷增長的，對他們的國民生產總值有非常誇大的觀點，同時低估了投入軍事的資源規模。

--- 段落 274 (441 字元) ---
See, it was explained to them, “How was it that in this somewhat smaller economy, let’s say half ours, they could spend six percent of their GNP and have a  military establishment which in many ways was competitive with ours?” We were  spending five percent of our GNP.Well, they would say we don’t have complex  economic arguments about how…though they were more efficient in those  industries of that sort.- Q2: Capture economies of scale.

[翻譯]
他們被解釋說："在這個規模較小的經濟體系中，他們如何能夠花費他們國民生產總值的百分之六來建立一支軍隊，而這支軍隊在很多方面都和我們的競爭力相當？"我們當時只花費我們國民生產總值的百分之五。他們可能會說，他們沒有複雜的經濟論點來...儘管在某些行業方面他們更高效率。- 問題二：抓住規模經濟。

--- 段落 278 (416 字元) ---
This talk is great for one primary  reason: The conventional view of the relationship of the RAND analytical community to the American defense establishment was that you have a bunch of military  officers who, for a variety of reasons, were pathological and ignore reality.And  yet a bunch of brilliant, objective scientists at RAND who [indistinct] perceived  reality, and you proceed to set the situation straight.

[翻譯]
這次演講之所以很棒，有一個主要原因：人們一直以為RAND分析社群與美國國防機構之間的關係是，有一群軍事將領們因為各種原因是病態的，忽略現實。然而在RAND有一群優秀客觀的科學家們，他們感知現實，並設法將情況理清。

--- 段落 279 (485 字元) ---
What you portray is a picture  of analysis as a social phenomenon, in which you have communities of people  at work on various problems.And reality and truth in these social communities  may be [indistinct] a generation.The Great Depression is one of them.World War  II is another event.The explosion in thermonuclear power is another event.And  the Cuban missile crisis is the fourth.There’s obviously others, but those seem to  be the four events over a period of maybe 30, 40 years.

[翻譯]
你描繪的是一幅關於分析作為一種社會現象的圖畫，在其中你可以看到社群中的人們努力解決各種問題。這些社會群體中的現實和真相可能在一代人之間產生變化。大蕭條是其中之一，第二次世界大戰是另一事件，熱核能爆炸是另一事件，古巴飛彈危機是第四個事件。顯然還有其他事件，但這些似乎是在大概30到40年的時間範圍內發生的四個事件。

--- 段落 280 (176 字元) ---
And once every 10, 15,  20 years something really comes and knocks in on these communities and kind  of forces them to sort of look out [indistinct] and reorient them slightly.

[翻譯]
每隔10、15、20年，某些事情真的會出現，打擾這些社區，迫使他們重新定位與重新調整。

--- 段落 281 (437 字元) ---

[翻譯]

[翻譯]

Robert Oppenheimer和洛斯阿拉莫斯的科學家，將軍萊斯利·格羅夫斯傾向於對這些人推行軍事規範。我不知道他的腦海中是否曾出現過這種想法...
- Q3：我不太確定，我對此不了解很多。我認為這也是一種過於簡化的描述。我的意思是，是萊斯利·格羅夫斯選擇了奧本海默。奧本海默並不是領先的候選人，該職位本應由詹姆斯·康納特擔任。康納特是"美國建制科學家先生"，是具有所有資格的人。

--- 段落 322 (464 字元) ---
And it’s clear from what  Groves thought at the time, “I know Conant, I know this other…Ernest Lawrence,  and I’ve never heard of Oppenheimer.” [Indistinct]…he’s the only person who can  make this whole program run.It’s Oppenheimer who always had very nice things  to say about Groves.[Indistinct; multiple voices]  
- Q7: …it was two other things.It was, number one, his ability to manage, which I  guess the other two, Lawrence and Conant, had also demonstrated.

[翻譯]
從當時格羅夫斯的想法來看，“我認識康納特，我認識這個其他人...歐內斯特·勞倫斯，我從來沒聽說過奧本海默。” [不清晰]...他是唯一能使整個計劃運行的人。奧本海默總是對格羅夫斯讚不絕口。 [不清晰；多個聲音]
- Q7：...還有另外兩件事。首先是他的管理能力，我想勞倫斯和康納特也已經證明了這一點。

--- 段落 323 (373 字元) ---
But there were a lot of frictions, too, between what Groves wanted to do with those people  and what Oppenheimer wouldn’t let him do with them.- Q3: Yeah, true.- Q7: When you were talking about earlier how to organize the book, are you looking  for something to organize the entire book?- Marshall: No, I think we have an idea about the organization of the book as a whole.

[翻譯]
但格羅夫斯想要與那些人做的事情之間也存在很多摩擦，而奧本海默則不讓他這樣做。-Q3:是的，這是真的。- Q7: 當你早些時候談到如何組織這本書時，你是在尋找一些將整本書組織起來的東西嗎？- 馬歇爾：不，我認為我們已經對整本書的組織有了一個想法。

--- 段落 324 (470 字元) ---
It’s how in each of these chapters to deal with this intellectual history, and then  there’s what was happening in the organization, in the immediate organization,  and what’s happening maybe more broadly [indistinct].- Q2: Organizing themes…  
- Marshall: …how to do that.- Q3: Well, there are at least three of them stressed: Andy’s intellectual development;  did it alter the analytical community at RAND; and then what the hell is going on  in the rest of the world?

[翻譯]
在每個章節中如何應對這種知識歷史，然後在組織中發生的事情，即組織中正在發生的事情，以及可能更廣泛地發生的事情。- 問題2：組織主題...
- 馬歇爾：...如何做到這一點。- 問題3：嗯，至少有三個重點：安迪的思想發展；它是否改變了蘭德分析社群；然後世界其他地方到底發生了什麼？

--- 段落 325 (492 字元) ---
Well, the real world, in terms of what people actually do.- Marshall: Yeah, right.- Q3: And that’s not such a [indistinct] thing to do.- Marshall: Now there will be later sessions on the ‘70s, ‘80s, early ‘90s, I guess—I  don’t know where to cut it off.- Q3: From a literary point of view, the way you did it today was effective.You say,  RAND in some sense reaches its culminating point of glory sometime around  1960.And then, “What was it like?” And then going back, “How did we get there?

[翻譯]
嗯，真實世界，就是指人們實際上所做的事情。- 馬歇爾：是的，沒錯。- Q3：這不是一件很容易做的事情。- 馬歇爾：現在將來會有關於70年代、80年代和90年代初的其他討論，我想我不知道怎麼結束。- Q3：從文學的角度來看，你今天的做法非常有效。你說，RAND在某種意義上在1960年左右達到了巔峰。然後，“那是什麼樣子？”然後回溯，“我們是如何到達那裡的？”

--- 段落 326 (287 字元) ---
”  From a story point of view it works.- Q7: Schlesinger once had a short comment—or at least it was attributed to him—  he said, “RAND was a dung heap, but sometimes in dung heaps roses grow.”  
- Q3: Unfortunately, there are lots of dung heaps.And roses.- Marshall: OK.Well, thank you.

[翻譯]
從故事觀點來看，這是行得通的。- Q7: 施萊辛格曾經發表過一則簡短的評論，或者至少是被歸因於他，他說，“RAND是一個糞堆，但有時在糞堆中也會長出玫瑰。”
- Q3: 不幸的是，有很多糞堆。還有玫瑰。- 馬歇爾: 好的。謝謝你。

--- 段落 373 (318 字元) ---
37 To help devise strategies for the efficient and effective use of nuclear weapons, the Air Force  in 1946 created an independent organization—designated Project RAND and located within  the Douglas Aircraft Company—to conduct research on intercontinental air warfare.By 1948,  the arrangement was proving unworkable.

[翻譯]
為了幫助制定有效且高效使用核武器的策略，空軍在1946年成立了一個獨立的組織——名為RAND計畫，位於道格拉斯飛機公司，進行有關洲際空戰的研究。到了1948年，這個安排已被證明行不通。

--- 段落 374 (439 字元) ---
Existing and prospective RAND employees were  leery of working for a subsidiary of an aircraft manufacturer rather than a truly independent  organization, and other aerospace firms began to protest that the existence of RAND gave  Douglas an unfair advantage in the competition for government contracts.Consequently,  RAND officials created an independent nonprofit corporation, the RAND Corporation, to  house Project RAND and its assets.

[翻譯]
現有和潛在的蘭德公司員工對於在一家航空製造商的子公司工作感到懷疑，而不是一個真正獨立的組織，其他航空航天公司開始抗議認為蘭德的存在使得道格拉斯公司在競爭政府合同時具有不公平的優勢。因此，蘭德公司官員創建了一個獨立的非營利機構，蘭德研究院，以容納蘭德項目及其資產。

--- 段落 375 (461 字元) ---
The RAND research agenda was broad, but at its core  was an effort to “make a major scientific attack on the whole theory of warfare, in the broadest  sense of the words.”RAND quickly became one of the nation’s leading centers for research on  nuclear strategy and policy.It also conducted pioneering work in rocketry and space systems,  digital computing, and artificial intelligence.Some of its most influential work was in applied  mathematics and economics.

[翻譯]
RAND研究議程涵蓋範圍廣泛，但其核心是“對戰爭整個理論進行重大科學攻擊，這是字義上最廣泛的意義。”RAND很快成為國家頂尖的核戰略和政策研究中心之一。它還在火箭技術和太空系統、數位運算以及人工智慧方面進行了開創性工作。它最有影響力的一些工作是應用數學和經濟學。

--- 段落 376 (498 字元) ---
RAND analysts made advances in game theory, modeling and  simulation, cost analysis, and Monte Carlo methods as they sought to improve military decision-making.By the mid-1960s, RAND comprised over 1,100 employees and conducted more  than $23 million of funded research annually.Project RAND Second Annual Report, RA-15075  (1 Mar 1948), 3, quoted in Andrew David May, “The RAND Corporation and the Dynamics  of American Strategic Thought, 1946-1962” (PhD diss., Emory University, 1998) 23.David R.

[翻譯]
安德魯·大衛·梅（Andrew David May）在他於1998年在埃默里大學完成的博士論文中指出，蘭德分析師在改進軍事決策過程中取得了博弈論、建模和模擬、成本分析以及蒙特卡羅方法等方面的進展。到了1960年代中期，蘭德公司已擁有超過1,100名員工，每年進行的研究經費超過2300萬美元。這則信息摘自蘭德計劃評估中心第二屆年度報告（RA-15075，1948年3月1日的報告）。

That all changed in May of 1960, when the  Soviets shot down one of the CIA’s U-2 spy planes on its way to photograph a missile testing  center at Plesetsk.Not long afterward, Marshall remembers, a Rand analyst stopped him one  day in the parking lot and said, ‘Now I understand what you and Loftus were talking about.’”  Thomas Powers, “Choosing a Strategy for World War III,” The Atlantic Monthly, 250, no.5  (Nov 1982): 91.

[翻譯]
一切都在1960年5月發生了變化，當時蘇聯擊落了一架 CIA 的 U-2 間諜飛機，這架飛機要前往拍攝位於普列焦茨克的導彈測試中心。不久之後，馬歇爾回憶說，一名蘭德分析師在停車場裡拦住他，說：“現在我明白你和羅夫特斯當時在談什麼了。”（摘自 Thomas Powers 的《為第三次世界大戰選擇戰略》，《大西洋月刊》1982年11月號第250期第91頁。）
